				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_US&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="T-Mobile US">T-Mobile US</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">It has been requested that the title of this article be changed to <i><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_US&amp;redirect=no">T-Mobile US</a></span></i>.  Please see <a href="/wiki/Talk:T-Mobile_USA#Requested_move_10_April_2020" title="Talk:T-Mobile USA">the relevant discussion</a>.  The page <b>should not be moved</b> unless the discussion is <em>closed</em> with a summary describing the <em>consensus achieved</em> in support of the move.</div></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>T-Mobile USA, Inc.</b>, commonly shortened to <b>T-Mobile</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Cellular_network" title="Cellular network">wireless network operator</a>; its largest shareholder is the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a> company <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> (DT) with a 43% share, with Japanese conglomerate holding company <a href="/wiki/SoftBank_Group" title="SoftBank Group">SoftBank Group</a> partially owning the company as well at a 24% share. The remaining 33% share of the company is owned by the public through <a href="/wiki/Common_stock" title="Common stock">common stock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-4">[4]</a></sup> Its headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Bellevue,_Washington" title="Bellevue, Washington">Bellevue, Washington</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_metropolitan_area" title="Seattle metropolitan area">Seattle metropolitan area</a>. T-Mobile is the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Wireless_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Wireless carrier">wireless carrier</a> in the United States, with 86.0 million customers as of the end of Q4 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">T-Mobile USA, Inc.</caption><tbody><tr><td <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)<sup id="cite_ref-10-K_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-2">[2]</a></sup></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: href="#cite_note-:9-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div (business)">Divisions</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Metro_by_T-Mobile" title="Metro by T-Mobile">Metro by T-Mobile</a></li><li><a title="Dish Network">Dish Network</a> pending)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://t-mobile.com">t-mobile<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4q2012_results_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4q2012_results-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-overview2011_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview2011-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_2017_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K_2017-8">[8]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>T-Mobile USA provides wireless voice and data services in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a> under the T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Metro_by_T-Mobile" title="Metro by T-Mobile">Metro by T-Mobile</a> brands (which it acquired via the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Metro_PCS" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro PCS">Metro PCS</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_takeover" title="Reverse takeover">reverse takeover</a> in 2013, resulting in T-Mobile going <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a> on the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" class="mw-redirect" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> stock exchange), and also serves as the host network for many <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">mobile virtual network operators</a>. The company has annual revenues of over $40 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-10-K_2017_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K_2017-8">[8]</a></sup> In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a> named T-Mobile the number one American wireless carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>On April 1, 2020, T-Mobile USA and <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint Corporation</a> completed <a href="/wiki/Merger_of_Sprint_Corporation_and_T-Mobile_USA" title="Merger of Sprint Corporation and T-Mobile USA">their merger</a> with T-Mobile now being the whole owner of Sprint, making Sprint an effective subsidiary of T-Mobile until the Sprint brand is officially phased out. Leadership, background, and stock changes happened immediately, with customer side changes happening over time. No timeline has been released for these changes.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:13_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p>T-Mobile U.S. traces its roots to the 1994 establishment of <b>VoiceStream Wireless PCS</b> as a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Western_Wireless_Corporation" title="Western Wireless Corporation">Western Wireless Corporation</a>. After its spin off from parent Western Wireless on May 3, 1999, VoiceStream Wireless was purchased by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom AG</a> in 2001 for $35 billion and renamed T-Mobile USA, Inc, in July 2002. In 2013, T-Mobile and MetroPCS finalised a merger of the two companies which started trading as T-Mobile U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-vsw-tmo_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vsw-tmo-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj_att_purchase_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_att_purchase-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vs_spinoff_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vs_spinoff-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="VoiceStream_Wireless">VoiceStream Wireless</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: VoiceStream Wireless" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>VoiceStream Wireless PCS was established in 1994 as a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Western_Wireless_Corporation" title="Western Wireless Corporation">Western Wireless Corporation</a> to provide wireless personal communications services (PCS) in 19 FCC-defined metropolitan service areas in several western and southwestern states using the <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> digital wireless standard.<sup id="cite_ref-history_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-18">[18]</a></sup> VoiceStream Wireless' digital, urban service areas complemented the analog, rural service areas marketed by Western Wireless under the <a href="/wiki/Cellular_One" title="Cellular One">Cellular One</a> brand.<sup id="cite_ref-cellular_one_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cellular_one-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>Western Wireless spun off its VoiceStream Wireless division into a new company called VoiceStream Wireless Corporation in May 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-fcc_2001approve_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcc_2001approve-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Omnipoint_and_Aerial_acquisitions">Omnipoint and Aerial acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Omnipoint and Aerial acquisitions" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2000, VoiceStream Wireless acquired two regional GSM carriers. <b>Omnipoint Corporation</b>, a regional network operator in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern U.S.</a>, was acquired on February 25, 2000. <b>Aerial Communications Inc.;</b> a regional network operator in the Columbus, Houston, Kansas City, Minneapolis-St. Paul, Pittsburgh, and Tampa-St. Petersburg-Orlando markets; was acquired on May 4, 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup> The combined company retired the Omnipoint and Aerial brands and completed integrating the three companies by converting to a single customer billing platform, implementing standard business practices and launching the VoiceStream brand and "GET MORE" marketing strategy in all markets.<sup id="cite_ref-vsw_about_2002-04_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vsw_about_2002-04-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Deutsche_Telekom_acquires_VoiceStream_and_Powertel">Deutsche Telekom acquires VoiceStream and Powertel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Deutsche Telekom acquires VoiceStream and Powertel" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VoiceStream-T-Mobile_transitional_logo_circa_April_2002.gif" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/25/VoiceStream-T-Mobile_transitional_logo_circa_April_2002.gif" decoding="async" width="150" height="68" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="150" data-file-height="68"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 68px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/25/VoiceStream-T-Mobile_transitional_logo_circa_April_2002.gif" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="68" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VoiceStream-T-Mobile_transitional_logo_circa_April_2002.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Transitional logo used by VoiceStream prior to the 2001 re-branding to T-Mobile</div></div></div>
<p>On June 1, 2001, Deutsche Telekom (DT) completed the acquisition of VoiceStream Wireless Inc. for $35 billion and <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern U.S.</a> regional GSM network operator <a href="/wiki/Powertel_(U.S._cellular_carrier_1998-2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="Powertel (U.S. cellular carrier 1998-2001)">Powertel, Inc.</a> for $24 billion. By the end of 2001, VoiceStream Wireless had 19,000 employees serving 7 million subscribers.
</p><p>On September 2, 2001, VoiceStream Wireless Inc. adopted the name, <b>T-Mobile USA, Inc.</b> and began rolling out the T-Mobile brand, starting with locations in California and Nevada.<sup id="cite_ref-vsw_about_2002-08-05_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vsw_about_2002-08-05-23">[23]</a></sup> T-Mobile USA, Inc. was an operating entity of <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile International AG</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-overview2011_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview2011-7">[7]</a></sup> before becoming a direct subsidiary of Deutsche Telekom AG.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="SunCom_acquisition">SunCom acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: SunCom acquisition" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On September 17, 2007, the company announced the acquisition of regional GSM carrier <a href="/wiki/SunCom" title="SunCom">SunCom Wireless Holdings, Inc.</a> for $2.4 billion; the acquisition closed on February 22, 2008. By September 8, 2008, SunCom's operations were integrated with those of the company. The acquisition added SunCom's 1.1 million customers to the company's customer base and expanded the company's network coverage to include southern <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, eastern <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, northeastern <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>. Following the Suncom acquisition, T-Mobile possessed native network presence in all the major metro areas in the United States, making it a true nationwide carrier.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Aborted_acquisition_by_AT.26T"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aborted_acquisition_by_AT&amp;T">Aborted acquisition by AT&amp;T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Aborted acquisition by AT&amp;T" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Attempted_purchase_of_T-Mobile_USA_by_AT%26T" title="Attempted purchase of T-Mobile USA by AT&amp;T">Attempted purchase of T-Mobile USA by AT&amp;T</a></div>
<p>On March 20, 2011, DT accepted a $39 billion stock and cash purchase offer from <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">AT&amp;T</a> for the company. The acquisition was subject to regulatory approvals, a reverse breakup fee in certain circumstances, and customary regulatory and closing conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_att_purchase_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_att_purchase-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-attacq_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-attacq-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-att_acquires_tmobileusa_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-att_acquires_tmobileusa-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>If the merger had been completed, AT&amp;T Mobility would have had a customer base of approximately 130 million users, making it the largest wireless carrier in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_att_purchase_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_att_purchase-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>On August 31, 2011, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> issued to block AT&amp;T's merger with T-Mobile on the basis that it would "substantially lessen competition" in the wireless market.<sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ-28">[28]</a></sup>
Further reports indicated that the FCC would likely oppose the merger.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>On December 19, 2011, in the face of heavy resistance from the U.S. government, AT&amp;T CEO <a href="/wiki/Randall_Stephenson" class="mw-redirect" title="Randall Stephenson">Randall Stephenson</a> announced that the company had officially withdrawn its $39 billion bid.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In an official statement, Stephenson addressed the continuing spectrum shortage (due to a significant increase in wireless demand), hinting that the company will continue to seek other options to solve the shortage in the short term.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_MetroPCS_Communications">Merger with MetroPCS Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Merger with MetroPCS Communications" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On October 3, 2012, MetroPCS Communications reached an agreement to merge with T-Mobile USA. MetroPCS shareholders would hold a 26% stake in the company formed after the merger, which retained the T-Mobile brand. While the new company was still the fourth-largest carrier in the United States (at the time), the acquisition gave T-Mobile access to more spectrum and financial resources to maintain competitiveness and expand its LTE network.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The merger between T-Mobile USA Inc. and MetroPCS was officially approved by MetroPCS shareholders on April 24, 2013. The deal was structured as a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_takeover" title="Reverse takeover">reverse takeover</a>; the combined company went <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a> on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> as TMUS and became T-Mobile U.S. Inc. on May 1, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-approve_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-approve-33">[33]</a></sup> The merger agreement gave <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> the option to sell its 72% stake in the company formed by the merger and valued at around $14.2 billion to a third party before the end of the 18-month <a href="/wiki/Lock-up_period" title="Lock-up period">lock-up period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="The_.22Un-carrier.22.2C_additional_wireless_spectrum_acquisition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='The_"Un-carrier",_additional_wireless_spectrum_acquisition'>The "Un-carrier", additional wireless spectrum acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title='Edit section: The "Un-carrier", additional wireless spectrum acquisition' data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In March 2013, T-Mobile introduced a major overhaul of its plan structure, marketed by branding themselves as being "the Un-carrier". A new contract-free pricing structure with simpler plans was introduced in which a phone's cost is paid over a two-year financing plan.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-uncarrier_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-uncarrier-35">[35]</a></sup> The "Un-carrier" strategy has since been expanded to encompass other value-added services, such as a plan add-on allowing phone trade-ins for early upgrades twice per year,<sup id="cite_ref-verge-jumpgrade_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-jumpgrade-36">[36]</a></sup> carrying over unused data allotments for up to a year,<sup id="cite_ref-cnet-datastash_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet-datastash-37">[37]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Zero-rating" title="Zero-rating">zero-rating</a> of selected music and video services (the latter locked to "DVD quality") over the mobile network,<sup id="cite_ref-pcw-bingeon_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcw-bingeon-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> These moves came as part of an effort under new CEO <a href="/wiki/John_Legere" title="John Legere">John Legere</a> to help revitalize the business as it improves its network quality.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-uncarrier_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-uncarrier-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>Though this system is said to improve network quality, issues surrounding net neutrality infringement have also come to light. The type of <a href="/wiki/Zero-rating" title="Zero-rating">zero-rating</a> that is offered by T-Mobile allows it to charge higher rates to third-parties, meaning that <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">ISP</a> can prioritize the company that pays a higher premium. This makes it more difficult for smaller third-parties who are unable to pay the high premium charged by the ISP.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>On June 28, 2013, T-Mobile agreed to buy wireless spectrum for the Mississippi Valley region from its competitor <a href="/wiki/U.S._Cellular" title="U.S. Cellular">U.S. Cellular</a> for around $308 million, allowing it to expand its 4G network across 29 more markets.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>On January 6, 2014, T-Mobile signed agreements with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a> to purchase some 700 MHz A-Block spectrum licenses for $2.365 billion. Moreover, a transfer of some AWS and PCS spectrum licenses with a value of $950 million has been agreed upon by T-Mobile and Verizon. The acquisition reportedly gave T-Mobile additional coverage for approximately 158 million people in 9 of the top 10 and 21 of the top 30 U.S. markets.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_Sprint_Corporation">Merger with Sprint Corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Merger with Sprint Corporation" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Merger_of_Sprint_Corporation_and_T-Mobile_USA" title="Merger of Sprint Corporation and T-Mobile USA">Merger of Sprint Corporation and T-Mobile USA</a></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Wireless_networks">Wireless networks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Wireless networks" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>The company owns licenses to operate a cellular communications network in the 1900 MHz (PCS) and 1700 MHz (AWS) bands with coverage in many parts of the continental U.S., Alaska, Hawaii, Puerto Rico, and the U.S. Virgin Islands, as well as licenses in the 700 MHz band (block A mostly) available in certain parts of the country. In 2017 T-Mobile also acquired a nationwide 600 MHz license. It expects to deploy this spectrum over the next few years as it is vacated by television stations across the country in stages. With respect to technology, depending on the location, in the 1900 MHz band it deploys <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Mobile_Telecommunications_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Mobile Telecommunications System">UMTS</a>/<a href="/wiki/Evolved_HSPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolved HSPA">HSPA+</a>, and/or <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> (<a href="/wiki/LTE_frequency_bands" title="LTE frequency bands">Band</a> 2); in the 1700 MHz band it deploys UMTS/HSPA+ and/or LTE (B4 and B66); and LTE-only in the 700 MHz (B12) and 600 MHz (B71) bands. Its LTE network also supports <a href="/wiki/VoLTE" class="mw-redirect" title="VoLTE">VoLTE</a>. It provides coverage in areas where it does not own <a href="/wiki/Radio_frequency" title="Radio frequency">radio frequency</a> spectrum licenses via roaming agreements with other operators of compatible networks.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Cellular_network">Cellular network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cellular network" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company's predecessor, VoiceStream Wireless, began building a regional, <a href="/wiki/2G" title="2G">2G</a>, 1900 MHz GSM, circuit-switched, digital cellular network in 1994 and first offered service in 1996 in <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>. From that starting point, the network has expanded in size through acquisitions of other cellular-network operators and additional spectrum purchases. The network has also expanded in capabilities through the introduction of new technologies. VoiceStream upgraded the 1900 MHz network to include packet switching via <a href="/wiki/General_Packet_Radio_Service" title="General Packet Radio Service">General Packet Radio Service</a> (GPRS), then increased packet-switched data transmission speeds via <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Data_Rates_for_GSM_Evolution" title="Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution">Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution</a>. In 2006, the company spent $4.2 billion to purchase 120 D, E or F block 1700 MHz AWS licenses<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and began rolling out <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> UMTS services in those frequency bands. The company upgraded network equipment and <a href="/wiki/Back-haul" class="mw-redirect" title="Back-haul">back-haul</a> capabilities to enable <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_Packet_Access" title="High Speed Packet Access">HSPA</a> (High Speed Packet Access), and later <a href="/wiki/Evolved_HSPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolved HSPA">HSPA+</a> and <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> services.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue,_WA.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue%2C_WA.jpg/220px-T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue%2C_WA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue%2C_WA.jpg/220px-T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue%2C_WA.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:T-Mobile_Headquarters_in_Bellevue,_WA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>T-Mobile US headquarters in Bellevue, WA</div></div></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Packet-switched_data_upgrade">Packet-switched data upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Packet-switched data upgrade" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Packet-switched data service first became available to users in the form of <a href="/wiki/General_Packet_Radio_Service" title="General Packet Radio Service">General Packet Radio Service</a> (GPRS). Packet-switched data speeds increased when <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Data_Rates_for_GSM_Evolution" title="Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution">Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution</a> (EDGE) was incorporated into the network. EDGE coverage was available within at least forty percent of the GSM footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>Both voice capacity and packet-switched data speed improved when 3G <a href="/wiki/Universal_Mobile_Telecommunications_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Mobile Telecommunications System">Universal Mobile Telecommunications System</a> (UMTS) equipment was installed in the network. On January 5, 2010, the company announced that it had upgraded its entire 3G network to HSPA 7.2 Mbit/s, an improvement from its previous peak of 3.6 Mbit/s. It also said that it planned to be the first U.S. carrier to deploy <a href="/wiki/Evolved_HSPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolved HSPA">HSPA+</a> across its network by mid-2010. The company had finished HSPA+ trials in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia, Pennsylvania</a>, and had begun deploying HSPA+ across its network.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="3G_upgrade_.2F_discontinuation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="3G_upgrade_/_discontinuation"><span id="3G_AWS_upgrade"></span>3G upgrade / discontinuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 3G upgrade / discontinuation" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In September 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) auctioned licenses in the first <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Wireless_Services" title="Advanced Wireless Services">Advanced Wireless Services</a> band. This band was an area of wireless <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum" title="Electromagnetic spectrum">spectrum</a>, half in the 1700 <a href="/wiki/MHz" class="mw-redirect" title="MHz">MHz</a> (1.7 <a href="/wiki/GHz" class="mw-redirect" title="GHz">GHz</a>) and half in the 2100 <a href="/wiki/MHz" class="mw-redirect" title="MHz">MHz</a> (2.1 <a href="/wiki/GHz" class="mw-redirect" title="GHz">GHz</a>) frequencies, that was already in use by government services. The spectrum was planned to become available after the government users migrated to different frequencies.
</p><p>The auction made numerous licenses available in overlapping market-areas, economic-areas, and regional levels. Each license was individually bid upon, and T-Mobile USA was the winner in 120 license auctions, at an aggregate price of $4.18 billion. As part of its winnings, T-Mobile USA gained nationwide coverage of 1.7 GHz and 2.1 GHz, with numerous areas being supplemented with additional licenses. Examples include New York City, Chicago, and Boston where T-Mobile USA acquired one-third (33 percent) of the available spectrum, or San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, and Miami where they acquired 45 percent of the available spectrum.<sup id="cite_ref-fcc_aws_results_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcc_aws_results-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>October 6, 2006, two weeks after confirming its winning bids, the company announced its intentions to create a <a href="/wiki/UMTS" title="UMTS">UMTS</a> third-generation, or <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a>, cellular network with the spectrum it had won. It said it would utilize and build on the experience of T-Mobile International's European subsidiaries, which already implemented 3G networks. At the time of initial roll-out, the company intended to offer 7.2 Mbit/s service, making the company's 3G network the fastest in the U.S. The upgrade was forecast to cost $2.6 billion, in addition to the $4.12 billion spent to acquire the spectrum licenses.<sup id="cite_ref-TMO_US_3G_announcement_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMO_US_3G_announcement-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In the same announcement, the company indicated it had already begun to deploy about half of the upgraded equipment, beginning in major markets such as New York City. With the equipment in place, it would be able to activate its network as soon as the government agencies vacated the spectrum. The company had hoped to have its network activated by mid-2007, but as of September 2007, the government users had not vacated the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Wireless_Services" title="Advanced Wireless Services">AWS</a> band.<sup id="cite_ref-TMO_US_3G_announcement_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMO_US_3G_announcement-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>The company began selling its first 3G-capable phone, the Nokia 6263, in November 2007 and announced in February 2008 that its 3G network would finally be activated "within the next few months".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and released in the New York City market on May 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>By 2009, the company had launched its 3G network in more than 200 markets, covering some 208 million points of presence (POPS).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Throughout 2015, T-Mobile began refarming UMTS/HSPA services from the original AWS band to their PCS band to expand bandwidth available for LTE. This rendered a select number of T-Mobile 3G devices inoperable on the 3G network.<sup id="cite_ref-fiercewireless.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiercewireless.com-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="HSPA.2FHSPA.2B_upgrade"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HSPA/HSPA+_upgrade">HSPA/HSPA+ upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: HSPA/HSPA+ upgrade" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On June 28, 2010, the company announced that it would begin to upgrade its network from HSPA+ 21 to HSPA+ 42 beginning sometime in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> T-Mobile marketed HSPA+ services as 4G.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="4G_LTE_upgrade">4G LTE upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 4G LTE upgrade" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On February 23, 2012, during the Q4 Earnings Call, T-Mobile laid out the future of their 4G upgrade path. They would roll out the <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> network on the AWS spectrum, and transition their HSPA+ network to the PCS band. To achieve compatibility with other networks and phones in the US, T-Mobile began this transition in March 2013, and the rollout of LTE is currently underway as T-Mobile expands to more markets.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Due to the failed acquisition of T-Mobile USA by AT&amp;T, T-Mobile USA received additional UMTS frequency band IV (AWS) spectrum. On March 26, 2013, T-Mobile began rolling out LTE in 7 markets: <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_metropolitan_area" title="Kansas City metropolitan area">Kansas City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>On August 21, 2012, the FCC approved a deal between T-Mobile and Verizon in which T-Mobile gained additional AWS spectrum licenses in 125 Cellular Market Areas.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>On February 25, 2014, T-Mobile announced in its Q4 2013 earnings call that its 4G LTE network covered 209 million people in 273 metro areas. They also planned to start rolling out their 700 MHz A-Block spectrum by the end of 2014, which by the end of the rollout would cover 158 million people. This spectrum led to improved LTE coverage overall in these areas, particularly indoors.<sup id="cite_ref-q4_earnings_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-q4_earnings-57">[57]</a></sup></p><p>On March 13, 2014, T-Mobile announced a new plan to upgrade its entire 2G/EDGE network to 4G LTE. They expected 50% to be done by the end of 2014, and it to be "substantially complete" by the middle of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-network_march_2014_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-network_march_2014-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>On December 16, 2014, T-Mobile announced during CEO <a href="/wiki/John_Legere" title="John Legere">John Legere</a>'s Un-carrier 8.0 interview that their <a href="/wiki/4G_LTE" class="mw-redirect" title="4G LTE">4G LTE</a> network covered 260 million people and their 700 MHz Band 12 LTE had been rolled out in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Springs">Colorado Springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> They expected to cover 280 million with LTE by mid-2015 and 300 million by the end of 2015. They also stated that they covered 121 metro areas with their Wideband LTE.<sup id="cite_ref-Network_Building_Un-carrier_Style_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Network_Building_Un-carrier_Style-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>On October 27, 2015, T-Mobile announced in its Q3 2015 earnings call that they covered over 300 million people with LTE, reaching their 2015 end of year goal months ahead of schedule.  They had 245 markets with Wideband (at least 15+15 MHz) LTE.  They also had 204 markets with Extended Range 700 MHz Band 12 LTE covering around 175 million people.  Their coverage map revealed that they now had new native LTE coverage in Montana, the Dakotas, Eastern West Virginia, and Northern Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-3Q_2015_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3Q_2015-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>On May 25, 2016, T-Mobile announced that it will be purchasing the 700Mhz A-block license (LTE band 12) for the Chicago metro area. When this transaction closes, together with several other pending 700Mhz license acquisitions, T-Mobile expects to possess 700Mhz licenses covering a total of 272 million people, or 84% of the US population – including 10 of the top 10 largest US metro areas. T-Mobile refers to its 700Mhz low-band network as 'Extended-range LTE' and claims it penetrates buildings and reaches out farther than its PCS and AWS only network.<sup id="cite_ref-chicagoB12_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagoB12-61">[61]</a></sup> In September 2016, T-Mobile launched 4x4 MIMO and 3 channel carrier aggregation allowing theoretical speeds of 400 Mbit/s, and also announced that the company's LTE network reaches over 312 million potential subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>In early 2017, T-Mobile purchased 45% of available 600 MHz spectrum in the US, covering 100% geographically of the US. They started the rollout of LTE on this band on August 15, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018 T-Mobile has stated they will not discontinue rollout and upgrades of LTE in favor of 5G. Instead, they will continue to grow and support their LTE network to work simultaneously with 5G.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5g30cities_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5g30cities-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5gcitiesfierce_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5gcitiesfierce-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>As of January 22, 2019, the LTE-Advanced upgrade has been deployed in 6,000 cities and towns.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>As of October 28, 2019, LTE now covers 326 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>As of February 6, 2020, the 600 MHz network reaches 8,900 cities and towns, covering 248 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="5G_NR_upgrade">5G NR upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 5G NR upgrade" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On February 26, 2018, T-Mobile announced it would roll out 5G to 30 cities by the end of 2018, with compatible handsets delivering early 2019. They also stated their 5G network will be able to work simultaneously with their 4G LTE network, delivering faster speeds and broader range.<sup id="cite_ref-5g30cities_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5g30cities-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5gcitiesfierce_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5gcitiesfierce-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>On June 25, 2018, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Networks" title="Nokia Networks">Nokia</a> completed their first bi-directional 5G NR transmission in the 28 GHz frequency compliant with <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">3GPP 5G New Radio (NR) standards,</a> showing a big step forward to building a nationwide 5G Network.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>On July 30, 2018, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Networks" title="Nokia Networks">Nokia</a> announced a $3.5 billion contract for equipment and software to build out a nationwide 5G network that will be compliant with <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">3GPP 5G New Radio (NR) standards</a>. The network will use the 600 MHz and 28 GHz frequency bands.<sup id="cite_ref-5gnokiadeal_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5gnokiadeal-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>On September 11, 2018, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a> announced a $3.5 Billion contract for equipment to build out a nationwide 5G network that will be compliant with <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">3GPP 5G New Radio (NR) standards</a>. The network will use the 600 MHz and 28 GHz frequency bands.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> This marks $7 Billion already invested in T-Mobiles 5G network, which will use both companies equipment.
</p><p>On November 20, 2018, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Networks" title="Nokia Networks">Nokia</a> completed their first downlink 5G NR transmission in the 600 MHz frequency compliant with <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">3GPP 5G New Radio (NR) standards</a> in Spokane, Washington. 28 GHz only reaches roughly 1 square mile (2.6 km<sup>2</sup>), whereas 600 MHz can reach hundreds of square miles. This marks one step closer to a rural 5G network, one highly sought improvement with 5G technology (high-speed data in rural areas).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p><p>On January 7, 2019, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a> completed the first audio and video call using a live <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">NR</a> network using 3 separate frequency bands; 600 MHz, 28 GHz, and 39 GHz. This was also the first live network test with successful uplink and downlink.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>On June 28, 2019, T-Mobile officially launched their 5G mmWave network with the launch of their first commercially available 5G NR device, the Galaxy S10 5G. The network has launched in 6 cities; <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">NYC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>On July 11, 2019, T-Mobile and <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a> completed their first n71 (600 MHz) data session in their lab in Bellevue, Washington on a commercial 5G modem, the <a href="/wiki/Snapdragon_(processor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Snapdragon (processor)">Snapdragon</a> X55, which is the first commercial 5G modem to feature the n71 band. However, the modem was pre-market and not in any commercially available device.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>On November 7, 2019, T-Mobile announced that it's 600 MHz 5G network will launch on December 6, 2019. The network will launch alongside the first 2 600 MHz 5G devices, the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung</a> <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series" title="Samsung Galaxy Note series">Galaxy Note</a> 10+ 5G and the <a href="/wiki/OnePlus" title="OnePlus">OnePlus</a> <a href="/wiki/OnePlus_7T" title="OnePlus 7T">7T</a> Pro 5G McLaren Edition.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:7_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>On December 2, 2019, T-Mobile officially launched its 600 MHz 5G network. It launched with an initial coverage of 200 million people and over 5,000 cities or towns.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Roaming">Roaming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Roaming" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>T-Mobile has roaming arrangements with a number of national and regional <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operators" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile network operators">mobile network operators</a>, including <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">AT&amp;T Mobility</a>.
</p><p>As of 2008, <a href="/wiki/Prepaid_mobile_phone" title="Prepaid mobile phone">prepaid</a> customers have almost all of the postpaid domestic roaming privileges and restricted international roaming to Canada and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, T-Mobile USA began removing AT&amp;T Mobility roaming coverage in many locations across the country, and updated its on-line coverage maps<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> to reflect the smaller coverage area. AT&amp;T Mobility roaming remains available in select locations, primarily on smaller carriers that were acquired by AT&amp;T Mobility after long-term roaming contracts were in place between T-Mobile and the smaller carriers, including Centennial Wireless and Edge Wireless.
</p><p>On June 29, 2010, the company launched voice service in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> on GSM via roaming agreement through <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.broadpointinc.com/">Broadpoint</a>. T-Mobile USA was scheduled to launch data service in Fall 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Also in 2010, T-Mobile US became a member of the <a href="/wiki/FreeMove" title="FreeMove">FreeMove</a> alliance.
</p><p>On October 9, 2013, T-Mobile announced Simple Global, a service included with eligible Simple Choice plans. This service allows one to roam in over 100 countries with unlimited text and speed-limited data, and make calls at $0.20/minute. High-speed data passes will be available for purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On March 7, 2014, T-Mobile announced this number will be increasing to 122 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> If one is connected to WiFi in one of these countries, and their phone supports WiFi calling, all calls and texts to and from the USA are free, and work the same as if they were on the cellular network.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>On July 15, 2015, T-Mobile launched Mobile Without Borders, a service included with all new T-Mobile plans and available as an add-on to grandfathered or promotional plans for $10. This service allows the user to use their normal voice, text message, and data allotments while roaming in Mexico and Canada. Most T-Mobile services are available while roaming, with the notable exception of using the data in one's Data Stash.
</p><p>In August 2015, T-Mobile joined the Competitive Carriers Association's Data Services Hub, enabling the company to expand roaming partnerships with over a dozen rural and regional carriers. Smaller carriers will now be able to access T-Mobile's LTE network for roaming and T-Mobile will be able to expand roaming partnerships and extend its footprint with members whose network technologies had previously been incompatible.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2017, T-Mobile announced that starting November 12, 2017, LTE-speeds will be limited at 5 GB (with speeds going at speeds at 128 kbit/s or 256 kbit/s on some plans) while data roaming in Canada and Mexico still remains unlimited. However, calling and texting in these countries still remain free from roaming charges.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> T-Mobile also announced a partnership with US Cellular in California, Iowa, Washington, and Wisconsin to expand 4G LTE coverage. Compatible device required.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_frequency_spectrum_chart">Radio frequency spectrum chart</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Radio frequency spectrum chart" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

<td>Available in pockets of select cities.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="T-Mobile_HotSpots"><span id="T-Mobile_HotSpots"></span>T-Mobile HotSpots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: T-Mobile HotSpots" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>T-Mobile has used the term "<i>Hotspot</i>" to represent various products and technologies.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Wi-Fi_network_.28public.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wi-Fi_network_(public)">Wi-Fi network (public)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Wi-Fi network (public)" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The company operates a nationwide Wi-Fi Internet access network under the T-Mobile HotSpots brand. The T-Mobile HotSpots network consists of thousands of Wi-Fi access points installed in businesses, hotels, and airports throughout the U.S.
</p><p>The T-Mobile HotSpot service offers access to a nationwide network of approximately 8,350 access points, installed in venues such as <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> coffeehouses, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Office" title="FedEx Office">FedEx Office</a> Office and Print Centers, <a href="/wiki/Hyatt" title="Hyatt">Hyatt</a> hotels and resorts, <a href="/wiki/Red_Roof_Inns" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Roof Inns">Red Roof Inns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofitel" title="Sofitel">Sofitel</a> hotels, <a href="/wiki/Novotel" title="Novotel">Novotel</a> hotels, the airline clubs of <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, as well as airports.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>The T-Mobile HotSpots network can be traced to the company's 2002 purchase of bankrupt wireless <a href="/wiki/ISP" class="mw-redirect" title="ISP">ISP</a> <a href="/wiki/MobileStar" title="MobileStar">MobileStar</a>, which began building its network in 1998. After completing the purchase, the company expanded the network into 400 <a href="/wiki/Borders_Group" title="Borders Group">Borders</a> bookstores, as well as 100 of the most-frequented airport clubs and lounges operated by American Airlines, Delta Air Lines, and United Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>On September 14, 2014, T-Mobile partnered up with GoGo to provide free texting on airplanes for its customers. GoGo services are provided on Delta Airlines, American Airlines, United Airlines and Alaska Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>On June 6, 2016, T-Mobile expanded its partnership with GoGo to offer T-Mobile users one hour of free WiFi on customers phones while T-Mobile One Plus and One Plus International users also get free WiFi throughout the entire flight. T-Mobile also included other messaging apps (iMessage, Google Hangouts, WhatsApp and Viber) in addition to SMS texting being provided since September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Wi-Fi_network_.28private.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wi-Fi_network_(private)">Wi-Fi network (private)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Wi-Fi network (private)" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>T-Mobile has also used the term to describe Wi-Fi Access Points that it sold to end users to expand their cell phone network to phones equipped to also receive Wi-Fi using a <a href="/wiki/VOIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VOIP">VOIP</a>-like technology.  (The models included at least two by <a href="/wiki/Linksys" title="Linksys">Linksys</a>: the WRTU54G-TM and the WRT54G-TM and one by <a href="/wiki/D-Link" title="D-Link">D-Link</a>: the TM-G5240.)
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>For the fiscal year 2017, T-Mobile US reported earnings of US$4.481 billion, with an annual revenue of US$40.604 billion, an increase of 8.3% over the previous fiscal cycle. T-Mobile's shares traded at over $62 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$58.1 billion in November 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
