</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Products and services" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Magenta_.26_Magenta_Plus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Magenta_&amp;_Magenta_Plus">Magenta &amp; Magenta Plus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Magenta &amp; Magenta Plus" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On June 2, 2019 T-Mobile announced the launch of Magenta and Magenta Plus plans to phase out and replace the T-Mobile ONE family of plans. The Magenta family of plans build on the existing features of the T-Mobile ONE and ONE Plus plans, but now include additional features like 3GB of Mobile HotSpot Data for standard Magenta plans, and retaining the same enhanced HD Streaming, 20GB of Mobile HotSpot Data, and other features of the T-Mobile ONE Plus plans.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Military.2C_First_Responder.2C_and_Unlimited_55.2B"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Military,_First_Responder,_and_Unlimited_55+">Military, First Responder, and Unlimited 55+</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Military, First Responder, and Unlimited 55+" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Alongside the T-Mobile Magenta family of plans are the specialized plans offered to Military personnel, First Responders, and seniors age 55 and up.
</p><p>Military and First Responder plans allow for qualified service members to receive 50% off of standard pricing Magenta and Magenta Plus plans. Customers must verify their affiliation within 45 days of activation or switching to the plan in order to retain the discounted offer.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p><p>The Unlimited 55+ allows customers at or over the age of 55 to receive a set discounted price on standard rate plans, however these accounts are limited to only 2 lines per account. Certain customers were permitted to add a third line to their account during a specific promotional period.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="T-Mobile_ONE_w.2F_ONE_Plus_Family"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="T-Mobile_ONE_w/_ONE_Plus_Family">T-Mobile ONE w/ ONE Plus Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: T-Mobile ONE w/ ONE Plus Family" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In August 2018, T-Mobile introduced T-Mobile ONE w/ ONE Plus Family plan, which allows HD streaming and adds 20 GB of mobile hotspot at 4G LTE speeds, and Name ID.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="T-Mobile_ONE">T-Mobile ONE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: T-Mobile ONE" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In August 2016, T-Mobile introduced T-Mobile ONE. It will be the only rate plan offered in the future, with plans to gradually phase out Simple Choice.<sup id="cite_ref-explore.t-mobile.com_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explore.t-mobile.com-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The plan has been criticized by the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a> and others for potentially violating <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">net neutrality</a> rules and making previously-included features paid extras.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>As of June 2, 2019, the T-Mobile ONE and ONE w/ ONE Plus Family plans have been retired and replaced by the new Magenta plans.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="T-Mobile_Essentials">T-Mobile Essentials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: T-Mobile Essentials" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The T-Mobile Essentials plan provides customers Unlimited Talk, Text, and Data service at a lower price than a standard Magenta or Magenta Plus plan. However, the Essentials plan does not include taxes and fees as the Magenta and Magenta Plus plans do. It also allows T-Mobile to "prioritize" Essentials customers data usage on the network at any time during network congestion or peak times.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Netflix_On_US">Netflix On US</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Netflix On US" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>T-Mobile offers any customer on a Magenta or Magenta Plus plan with 2 or more lines to participate in the Netflix on Us offer, essentially covering the cost of one standard Netflix subscription in the plan. Customers have the option to upgrade their subscription to Netflix's premium service for an additional cost, which will be added to the customer's T-Mobile bill.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Simple_Choice">Simple Choice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Simple Choice" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In March 2013, T-Mobile introduced a new streamlined plan structure known as <b>Simple Choice</b> for new customers. This is part of an initiative called <i><a href="/wiki/Un-carrier" title="Un-carrier">Un-carrier</a></i> which drops contracts, subsidized phones, overage fees for data, and early termination fees.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-uncarrier_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-uncarrier-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Capping_unlimited_data_users">Capping unlimited data users</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Capping unlimited data users" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 31, 2015, T-Mobile announced it will ask users who abuse its unlimited on-smartphone data plan by violating T-Mobile's Terms &amp; Conditions regarding <a href="/wiki/Tethering" title="Tethering">tethering</a> (which like unlimited on-smartphone data, remains unlimited, but offers a 14 <a href="/wiki/Gigabyte" title="Gigabyte">GB</a> high-speed allotment before throttling takes effect), by permanently removing user access to unlimited plans and migrating users to a tiered data plan. By doing so, all plans after a select amount of inclusive high-speed data, result in automatic throttled speeds, preventing unlimited high-speed tethering use and abuse of the network. T-Mobile stated that there are a small handful of users who abuse the tethering plan by altering device software and/or the use of an <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> app that masks T-Mobile's ability monitoring whether data is on-smartphone, or through smartphone mobile hotspot (tethering) by mimicking all data as on-smartphone use, with some customers abusing the service by using as much as 2 <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" title="Terabyte">TB</a> per month, causing speed issues for all other customers.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="InReach_program">InReach program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: InReach program" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The InReach program<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> provides a free cell phone and a limited number of voice minutes each month for <a href="/wiki/Low-income" class="mw-redirect" title="Low-income">low-income</a>-eligible families (one per family) who do not use Lifeline services offered by any other phone or wireless company.  It is funded through the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Service_Fund" title="Universal Service Fund">Universal Service Fund</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> but is only operational in a limited number of states and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro_by_T-Mobile">Metro by T-Mobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Metro by T-Mobile" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metro_by_T-Mobile" title="Metro by T-Mobile">Metro by T-Mobile</a></div>
<p>The former MetroPCS was taken over by T-Mobile in 2013, the new company formed T-Mobile US and currently continues to offer <a href="/wiki/Prepaid_mobile_phone" title="Prepaid mobile phone">prepaid</a> wireless services under the Metro by T-Mobile brand.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="GoSmart_Mobile">GoSmart Mobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: GoSmart Mobile" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>GoSmart Mobile was a T-Mobile branded service that launched in <a href="/wiki/Betaware" class="mw-redirect" title="Betaware">beta</a> on December 7, 2012, and became officially available nationwide on February 19, 2013. GoSmart offered no-contract SIM wireless services. GoSmart Mobile was sold to consumers through dealers who worked as independent contractors under their own company name. Such sellers are known as "Authorized Dealers" with either physical or online stores. In September 2016, T-Mobile sold the brand and 326,000 GoSmart Mobile customers to <a href="/wiki/TracFone_Wireless" title="TracFone Wireless">TracFone Wireless</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The customers were reclassified as wholesale subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking_cards">Banking cards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Banking cards" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On January 22, 2014, T-Mobile announced that it would expand its products into banking. T-Mobile would provide Visa card with banking features and a smartphone money management application with reduced-fee or zero-cost services for T-Mobile wireless customers. In addition, customers would have access to over 42,000 ATMs with no fees.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>In early 2016 T-mobile decided to discontinue the banking cards. They can no longer be purchased at T-Mobile.
</p><p>In early 2019 T-mobile released T-Mobile Money, an online banking option.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="TVision_Home">TVision Home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: TVision Home" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On December 13, 2017, T-Mobile US announced its intent to acquire the <a href="/wiki/IPTV" class="mw-redirect" title="IPTV">IPTV</a> provider Layer3 TV, which operates in Chicago and Washington, as the basis of its own subscription television service initially planned to launch in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>On April 10, 2019, T-Mobile officially announced the re-branding and re-launch of Layer3 TV as <b>TVision Home</b><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>The service has been criticized for mirroring the hardware, packaging, and pricing models of other linear television providers, with no meaningful differentiation in services or disruptive pricing models like T-Mobile's wireless services.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_service">Customer service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Customer service" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford,_CT.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford%2C_CT.jpg/220px-T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford%2C_CT.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2181" data-file-height="1404"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 142px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford%2C_CT.jpg/220px-T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford%2C_CT.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="142" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:T-Mobile_Store_in_Hartford,_CT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>T-Mobile Store in Hartford, Connecticut</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_of_experts">Team of experts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Team of experts" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2018, T-Mobile officially announced its new customer care concept called Team of Experts. The premise being customers never being transferred to another department. All representatives are trained billing, payment arrangements, and cancellations when in the past each had their own separate department. In addition to being cross-trained, the Team of Experts, which consists of usually between 30 and 35 account reps, 4 to 6 technical support representatives, 4 supervisors overseeing the representatives, and one manager, are assigned specific markets, usually within the region, the call center is in.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Awards" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>From as early as 2004, the company has captured multiple <a href="/wiki/J._D._Power_and_Associates" class="mw-redirect" title="J. D. Power and Associates">J. D. Power</a> annual awards in the areas of retail sales satisfaction, wireless customer care, and overall customer satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-overview2011_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview2011-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2011, J. D. Power and Associates stated that T-Mobile retail stores achieved the highest ratings among major wireless carriers for customer satisfaction for the fourth consecutive year, performing particularly well in price and promotions.<sup id="cite_ref-jdp_retailsatisfaction_2011_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdp_retailsatisfaction_2011-147">[147]</a></sup> Also in 2011, J. D. Power and Associates ranked T-Mobile USA highest among major providers in wireless customer care for the second consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-jdp_customercare_2011_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdp_customercare_2011-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>On December 3, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a> named T-Mobile the number one American wireless service provider. The results combine data from customer service, voice quality, text messaging services, and data speeds.<sup id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>On February 6, 2016, T-Mobile was awarded the JD Power Award for customer satisfaction in the full-service wireless category for the second year in a row. T-Mobile received the highest score ever in the wireless industry.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>In 2019, T-Mobile was recognized as one of Fortune's Top 100 Companies To Work For, ranking #49.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Outages">Outages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Outages" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sidekick_data_outage">Sidekick data outage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sidekick data outage" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_data_loss_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft data loss 2009">Microsoft data loss 2009</a></div>
<p>On October 1, 2009, some users of Microsoft's Sidekick handset temporarily lost personal data, including contacts, notes, and calendars. On October 8, most data services were restored to users.  The company and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> announced on October 10 that Sidekick device data "almost certainly has been lost as a result of a server failure at Microsoft/Danger."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> On October 15, Microsoft said it had been able to recover most or all data and would begin to restore it.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_sidekick_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_sidekick-153">[153]</a></sup> A few weeks later, all Sidekick customers were able to recover their data via Danger's sync website using a restore file or had the option to wait until data was restored to the device itself.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Network_outages">Network outages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Network outages" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On November 9, 2009, some of the company's subscribers temporarily lost the ability to send and receive <a href="/wiki/Telephone_call" title="Telephone call">calls</a> and text messages for several hours.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The company confirmed the outage via Twitter. The company stated that approximately five percent of its subscribers had been affected. It claimed that the problem was caused by a system software error.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p><p>On February 13 and March 25, 2015, T-Mobile suffered LTE outages along the east coast causing users to lose data connections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On May 8, 2018, subscribers throughout <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> experienced an approximately four-hour interruption in service caused by damage to a <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">fiber-optic cable</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Marketing" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harmon_Corner_2.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Harmon_Corner_2.jpg/220px-Harmon_Corner_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="3120"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Harmon_Corner_2.jpg/220px-Harmon_Corner_2.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harmon_Corner_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A T-Mobile advertisement at <a href="/wiki/Harmon_Corner" title="Harmon Corner">Harmon Corner</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jamie_Lee_Curtis" title="Jamie Lee Curtis">Jamie Lee Curtis</a> was the spokesperson for T-Mobile USA's predecessor, VoiceStream Wireless, since 1998. VoiceStream's advertising slogan was: "Get more from life". During the transition to the T-Mobile brand, Jamie Lee Curtis continued as a spokesperson for a short time and the slogan was changed to "T-Mobile. Get More."
Starting in 2002, the company's spokesperson was <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Zeta-Jones" title="Catherine Zeta-Jones">Catherine Zeta-Jones</a> who was the main figure in its branding strategy. As of September 2006, Zeta-Jones had officially been dropped as the "face" of the company for its advertising campaigns due to a corporate rebranding strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The company also relied on rapper <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> as the spokesperson for its <a href="/wiki/Danger_Hiptop" title="Danger Hiptop">T-Mobile Sidekick</a> in a series of commercials late in 2004, the company also released a series of Sidekick phones known as the D-Wade Edition for basketball player <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a>.
</p><p>The company is also an official sponsor of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>, the NBA <a href="/wiki/Rookie_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="Rookie Challenge">Rookie Challenge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">Women's National Basketball Association</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Overwatch_League" title="Overwatch League">Overwatch League</a>
</p><p>In 2009, it changed its approach to advertising and moved from the "Get More" slogan to a "Stick Together" slogan to focus more on the personal aspect of staying together with those who matter the most to its customers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The slogan was also meant to promote its MyFaves calling-circle plan. With this, the company also ended its relationship with Zeta-Jones, and now use mainly non-celebrity spokespeople (though Dwyane Wade, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Barkley" title="Charles Barkley">Charles Barkley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Howard" title="Dwight Howard">Dwight Howard</a> are featured in some commercials, in association with the company's sponsorship of the NBA as official wireless provider).
</p><p>In late May 2009, Zeta-Jones was brought back as a company spokesperson to show customers how to pay less for their wireless plan in a new "Mobile Makeovers" advertising campaign that refers a customer to third-party comparison site BillShrink.com.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p><p>In late 2009, commercials for the <a href="/wiki/HTC_Magic" title="HTC Magic">T-Mobile MyTouch 3G</a> featured the song "<a href="/wiki/If_You_Want_to_Sing_Out,_Sing_Out" title="If You Want to Sing Out, Sing Out">If You Want to Sing Out, Sing Out</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Cat_Stevens" title="Cat Stevens">Cat Stevens</a><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> and celebrities such as <a href="/wiki/Chevy_Chase" title="Chevy Chase">Chevy Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molly_Shannon" title="Molly Shannon">Molly Shannon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dana_Carvey" title="Dana Carvey">Dana Carvey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Hammond" title="Darrell Hammond">Darrell Hammond</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Another commercial with the same song performed by a different artist showed <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avril_Lavigne" title="Avril Lavigne">Avril Lavigne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brad_Paisley" title="Brad Paisley">Brad Paisley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Carly_Foulkes" title="Carly Foulkes">Carly Foulkes</a> is the spokeswoman for the <a href="/wiki/HTC_Glacier" class="mw-redirect" title="HTC Glacier">myTouch 4G</a> in commercials that parody the <a href="/wiki/Get_a_Mac" title="Get a Mac">Get a Mac</a> campaign. The model is known for <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Ralph_Lauren" title="Rugby Ralph Lauren">Rugby Ralph Lauren</a> ads.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_carly_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat_carly-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
Although Foulkes is often identified with the color pink, T-Mobile actually has a color trademark for the color <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">magenta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> and markets itself using its corporate colors.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mobile" title="Virgin Mobile">Virgin Mobile</a> has, in turn, parodied the Carly Foulkes ads.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2010, the company launched "Kids are free till 2012" for family lines.
</p><p>On December 1, 2011, a group of 100 Chicago-area women, along with <a href="/wiki/Carly_Foulkes" title="Carly Foulkes">Carly Foulkes</a>, were featured in a flash-mob style performance at <a href="/wiki/Woodfield_Mall" title="Woodfield Mall">Woodfield Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Schaumburg,_Illinois" title="Schaumburg, Illinois">Schaumburg, Illinois</a>, where the group, dressed in magenta dresses, sang and danced through the mall's atrium to their cover of <a href="/wiki/(There%27s_No_Place_Like)_Home_for_the_Holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="(There's No Place Like) Home for the Holidays">(There's No Place Like) Home for the Holidays</a>. The performance was filmed and edited into a holiday commercial, which was a success.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Un-carrier_movement">Un-carrier movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Un-carrier movement" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Starting in 2013, T-Mobile launched the <a href="/wiki/Un-carrier" title="Un-carrier">Un-carrier</a> marketing campaign. This movement introduced a slew of new tactics to offer consumers cheaper rate plans, cheaper global coverage, and several other benefits. T-Mobile CEO John Legere laid out an 'Un-Carrier manifesto' highlighting the approach and goals he wanted the company to pursue. One popular Un-carrier move features T-Mobile Tuesdays, where customers are offered a variety of free products and also able to win prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> The most recent Un-carrier campaign is titled 'T-Mobile One'. This is a new family plan offering, replacing all previous plans and is an all-inclusive unlimited plan, giving unlimited talk, text, and data. The only caveat being a video streaming on any device is limited to 480p resolution.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> CEO John Legere in an interview said "The biggest pain point that a million customers told me about is that they hate data buckets. And we had such success with Binge On that we wanted to turn our company into somebody that's selling a monthly subscription to the internet, all in, unlimited."<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> As of October 7, 2016, about a quarter of the overall account numbers have moved over to T-Mobile One, and about three-quarters of new postpaid accounts are activating on T-Mobile One.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_relations">Labor relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Labor relations" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>T-Mobile US employees and two labor unions have led multiple unionization attempts beginning as early as 2001.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_TU">Formation of TU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Formation of TU" data-section="46" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Hundreds of T-Mobile employees, with the backing of the <a href="/wiki/Communications_Workers_of_America" title="Communications Workers of America">Communications Workers of America</a> (CWA) and the German union <a href="/wiki/Ver.di" title="Ver.di">ver.di</a>, have joined together as <a href="/wiki/TU_(union)" title="TU (union)">TU</a> to gain representation at T-Mobile.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In July 2011, technicians in Connecticut, voted for representation by the Communications Workers of America-TU.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_tmo_response_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_tmo_response-175">[175]</a></sup> On September 25, 2013, MetroPCS workers in Harlem, NY, voted for a union voice and representation by CWA-TU.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_coordinated_organizing_effort">2009 coordinated organizing effort</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: 2009 coordinated organizing effort" data-section="47" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg/220px-Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="247"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 155px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg/220px-Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="155" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cohen_and_disguised_worker_at_press_conference_2010.09.22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CWA President Larry Cohen and a disguised, unidentified T-Mobile USA employee pictured at a 2009 press conference announcing a coordinated unionizing effort</div></div></div>
<p>In 2008, the CWA and ver.di launched a coordinated effort to unionize company employees. A spokesman for the CWA called on the company to stop resisting mobilization efforts and allow company employees to unionize as German employees of T-Mobile USA's parent company, DT, have done. In response, the company released an employee satisfaction study showing that more than seventy percent of the company's 40,000 workers were "very satisfied" with their jobs. Through a spokesman, the company stated, "Despite the Communication Workers of America's periodic organizing efforts for more than nine years, no group of T-Mobile employees has ever chosen to be represented by a union. While our company is always striving to find ways to improve, year after year, employees continue to view T-Mobile as a good place to work where they have no need for, or interest in, a union."<sup id="cite_ref-2009_tmo_response_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_tmo_response-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_pressure">Political pressure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Political pressure" data-section="48" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2009, a number of politicians, in one case acting after lobbying efforts by CWA union activists, wrote letters to <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Obermann" title="René Obermann">René Obermann</a>, DT's chief executive officer, in an effort to influence T-Mobile USA's labor practices in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-cwaactivists_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cwaactivists-177">[177]</a></sup></p><p>In a March 13, 2009, letter, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> (D-MA) asked "why the company's approach to labor rights are different in Germany than in the United States". In an April 30, 2010, letter sent after lobbying by Communications Workers of America activists, 26 Democratic members of Congress called on DT to protect and respect workers' rights in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-cwaactivists_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cwaactivists-177">[177]</a></sup> A separate July 1, 2010, letter from seven Republicans addressed the same issue.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> On August 10, 2010, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Bob_Casey,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Casey, Jr.">Bob Casey</a> (D-PA) released a statement in support of the worker's efforts to organize a union at the company.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> In a letter, dated September 21, 2010, fifteen Californian <a href="/wiki/Members_of_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of Congress">Members of Congress</a> urged Obermann to take action and implement fair and equitable <a href="/wiki/Labor_relations" title="Labor relations">labor relations</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In a November 5, 2009, letter, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_DiNapoli" title="Thomas DiNapoli">Thomas DiNapoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Comptroller" title="New York State Comptroller">New York State Comptroller</a> and Trustee of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Common_Retirement_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="New York State Common Retirement Fund">New York State Common Retirement Fund</a>, stated concerns about "the potential impact on the value of T-Mobile that may result from a disenfranchised workforce and the associated negative publicity that may impact T-Mobile's profitability."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Reports">Reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Reports" data-section="49" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lowering_The_Bar_Cover_2010.09.22.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Lowering_The_Bar_Cover_2010.09.22.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="150" data-file-height="200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 200px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Lowering_The_Bar_Cover_2010.09.22.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="200" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lowering_The_Bar_Cover_2010.09.22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Cover image of a report written by John Logan and published in 2009 by <a href="/wiki/American_Rights_at_Work" title="American Rights at Work">American Rights at Work</a></div></div></div>
<p>On December 9, 2009, the non-profit organization <a href="/wiki/American_Rights_at_Work" title="American Rights at Work">American Rights at Work</a> published a report written by Prof. John Logan, Director of Labor Studies at <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_State_University" title="San Francisco State University">San Francisco State University</a>, titled <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100717142730/http://www.americanrightsatwork.org/dmdocuments/ARAWReports/loweringthebar_lowres.pdf">"Lowering the Bar or Setting the Standard? Deutsche Telekom's U.S. Labor Practices"</a>. The report details behavior by the company that the author perceives as anti-union including dissemination of anti-union materials, intimidation and threats directed at pro-union workers, "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Captive_audience_meetings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Captive audience meetings (page does not exist)">captive audience meetings</a>" and the retention of anti-union specialists.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> In the report, which is based on documents from the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board" title="National Labor Relations Board">National Labor Relations Board</a>, internal company memos and handbooks, and interviews with workers, Logan asserts that the company engaged in a systematic campaign to prevent employees from forming a union and that DT was guilty of operating by a double standard. He claims that Deutsche Telekom respects workers' rights in Germany, where it cooperates closely with unions, but mistreats workers in the United States and interferes with their right to organize.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="where does quotation start? (July 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p><p>On September 2, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> released a report written by Lance Compa titled "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.hrw.org/node/92719">A Strange Case: Violations of Workers' Freedom of Association in the United States by European Multinational Corporations</a>". The report concludes that "company policy has translated into practices that leave the workforce fearful about even seeking union representation."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> DT proclaims its adherence to international labor law and standards that are embodied in German domestic laws. But HRW found that "T-Mobile USA's harsh opposition to workers' freedom of association in the United States betrays Deutsche Telekom's purported commitment to social responsibility, impedes constructive dialogue with employee representatives, and in several cases, has violated <a href="/wiki/ILO" class="mw-redirect" title="ILO">ILO</a> and <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> labor and human rights standards".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Workplace_activities">Workplace activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Workplace activities" data-section="50" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>At the company's <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown, Pennsylvania</a>, call center, security guards were ordered by company managers to write up incident reports whenever union supporters appeared on nearby public grounds and to record the license plate numbers of employees who stopped to take leaflets. In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board" title="National Labor Relations Board">National Labor Relations Board</a> found that these activities violated Section 8(a)(1) of the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="National Labor Relations Act">National Labor Relations Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, company management in the Pacific Northwest and Southwest Retail Divisions sent a memorandum to store managers instructing them to immediately report any union activity to their supervisors.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Human Rights Watch states, "The NLRB has long held that such activity interferes with, restrains, and coerces employees in the exercise of Section 7 rights in violation of workers' right to freedom of association."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_2">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Awards" data-section="51" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>T-Mobile has received multiple workplace awards. T-Mobile received a score of 100 on the Disability Equality Index (DEI), which measures disability inclusion. They were also named the Best Place to Work for LGBT Equality by the Human Rights Campaign for four consecutive years. T-Mobile was also awarded a Designation for the top 100 Military Friendly Employer by Military Friendly in 2017 for the tenth time. It was recognized as one of the World's Most Ethical Companies by the <a href="/wiki/Ethisphere_Institute" title="Ethisphere Institute">Ethisphere Institute</a> for the ninth year in a row. In addition to national awards, T-Mobile has also won local awards in many locations, including the best place to work in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita, Kansas</a> where the company has call centers located.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> On February 16, 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a> announced their 100 best companies to work for, naming T-Mobile 86th.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> On July 24, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Forbes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes.com">Forbes</a> ranked T-Mobile 182nd on their top 300 Best Places to Work for Women list.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_security">Information security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Information security" data-section="52" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>Nicolas Jacobsen was charged with intruding into the company's internal network in January 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Reports indicated that for about a year Jacobsen had access to customer passwords, e-mail, address books, <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_number" title="Social Security number">Social Security numbers</a>, birth dates, and <a href="/wiki/Danger_Hiptop" title="Danger Hiptop">Sidekick</a> photos. Affected customers included members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">United States Secret Service</a>. Secret Service informant identified Jacobsen as part of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080916201228/http://www.ustreas.gov/usss/press/pub2304.pdf">"Operation Firewall"</a> which provided evidence that Jacobsen had attempted to sell customer information to others for identity theft. T-Mobile USA and the Secret Service did not elaborate on the methods Jacobsen used to gain access but sources close to the case indicated that Jacobsen exploited an unpatched flaw in the <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Weblogic_Server" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Weblogic Server">Oracle WebLogic Server</a> application software used by the company.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Additional <a href="/wiki/SQL_injection" title="SQL injection">SQL injection</a> vulnerabilities with the company's web site were reported by Jack Koziol of the InfoSec Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p><p>T-Mobile offers access to voicemail without the input of a password by default. Parties acting in bad faith may be able to access such voice mailboxes via <a href="/wiki/Caller_ID_spoofing" title="Caller ID spoofing">Caller ID spoofing</a>. To avoid this possibility, T-Mobile recommends that all customers password-protect their mailboxes, but still offers the no password configuration by default due to customer demand.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p><p>On June 6, 2009, a message posted from an email account "pwnmobile_at_Safe-mail.net" to the Full Disclosure mailing list claimed that the company's network had been breached and showed sample data. The sender offered "databases, confidential documents, scripts and programs from their servers, financial documents up to 2009" to the highest bidder.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> On June 9, the company issued a statement confirming the breach but stating that customer data was safe. It claimed to have identified the source document for the sample data and believe it was not obtained by hacking.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> A later statement claimed that there was not any evidence of a breach.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy_and_surveillance">Privacy and surveillance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Privacy and surveillance" data-section="53" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>T-Mobile USA received a portion of the 1.3 million largely warrantless law enforcement requests for subscriber information (including text messages and phone location data) made in 2011, but refused to state how many requests it received.<sup id="cite_ref-Wired-massive-surveillance_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wired-massive-surveillance-199">[199]</a></sup> It did say that in the last decade, the number of requests have increased by 12 to 16 percent annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Register-snooping_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Register-snooping-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_retention_policies">Data retention policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Data retention policies" data-section="54" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to T-Mobile's privacy policy highlights, "Retention and Disposal", information is retained for as long as there is business or tax need or as applicable laws, regulations, or government orders require. T-Mobile notes that it disposes of Personal Information,  uses reasonable procedures designed to erase or render it unreadable (for example, shredding documents and wiping electronic media).<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, the Department of Justice (DOJ) released a document entitled, "Retention Periods of Major Cellular Providers," to advise law enforcement agents seeking to obtain cell phone records. This document was uncovered by the ACLU's coordinated records request on cell phone location tracking by police. Notably, the document showed that T-Mobile subscriber information was retained for 5 years and call detail records were kept for 2 years (prepaid) and 5 years (postpaid).<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, Massachusetts Sen. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Markey" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Markey">Edward Markey</a> revealed responses from the top four U.S. wireless providers as well as U.S. Cellular, C Spire, and Cricket/Leap Wireless, to his inquiry regarding user information disclosed to law enforcement officials. The following was T-Mobile's response regarding data retention: T-Mobile US retains customers' historic cell site information and cell tower dump information (180 days); call details records (7–10 years); text message content, data requests, and geo-location data not stored; voicemail content (up to 21 days); subscriber information (6 years after the account is closed).<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p><p>Comparing the 2010 DOJ memo released by the ACLU and Markey's 2013 wireless data retention disclosures, T-Mobile increased the retention period for subscriber information from 5 to 6 years. T-Mobile also increased its call detail record retention from 2 years (prepaid) and 5 years (postpaid) to 7–10 years.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="55" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=T-Mobile_USA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: References" data-section="56" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
